<p><a name="Demography" id="Demography"></a></p>
<h2><span class="editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a>]</span> <span class="mw-headline">Demography</span></h2>
<dl>
<dd>
<div class="noprint"><i>Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_Italy" title="Demography of Italy">Demography of Italy</a></i></div>
</dd>
</dl>
<p><a name="Population" id="Population"></a></p>
<h3><span class="editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a>]</span> <span class="mw-headline">Population</span></h3>
<p>The latest population estimate done by <a href="/wiki/ISTAT" title="ISTAT">ISTAT</a> (Italian Statistics Office) stated that there were 59,131,287 inhabitants in Italy in December 2006<a href="http://demo.istat.it/bilmens2006/index.html" class="external autonumber" title="http://demo.istat.it/bilmens2006/index.html" rel="nofollow">[9]</a>, making it the fourth largest population in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (after Germany, France and the United Kingdom), and the 22nd in the world. Gradual increase of population is mainly supplemented by immigrants and an increase in life expectancy of 79.81 years<a href="https://cia.gov/cia//publications/factbook/geos/it.html#People" class="external autonumber" title="https://cia.gov/cia//publications/factbook/geos/it.html#People" rel="nofollow">[10]</a>. Despite population growth, Italy is rapidly ageing. One in five Italian inhabitants is a pensioner; if this ageing trend continues, the Italian population could shrink by a quarter by 2050.<a href="http://72.14.205.104/search?q=cache:uYQDug_VVgEJ:www.un.org/esa/population/publications/migration/italy.pdf+Italy%27s+population+40+million+by+2050&amp;hl=en&amp;gl=ca&amp;ct=clnk&amp;cd=2" class="external autonumber" title="http://72.14.205.104/search?q=cache:uYQDug_VVgEJ:www.un.org/esa/population/publications/migration/italy.pdf+Italy%27s+population+40+million+by+2050&amp;hl=en&amp;gl=ca&amp;ct=clnk&amp;cd=2" rel="nofollow">[11]</a></p>
<p>Italy has the fifth highest population density in all of Europe with 196 persons per square kilometre. The highest density is in Northwestern Italy, as two regions out of twenty (Lombardy and Piedmont) combined, contain one quarter of the Italian population, where an estimated 7.4 million people live in the metropolitan <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> area<a href="http://213.253.134.43/oecd/pdfs/browseit/0406041E.PDF" class="external autonumber" title="http://213.253.134.43/oecd/pdfs/browseit/0406041E.PDF" rel="nofollow">[12]</a>. The literacy rate in Italy is 98% overall, and school is mandatory for children aged 6 to 18.<sup id="_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#_note-5" title="">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p><a name="Largest_cities" id="Largest_cities"></a></p>

<p><a name="Metropolitan_areas" id="Metropolitan_areas"></a></p>
<h4><span class="editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Metropolitan areas">edit</a>]</span> <span class="mw-headline">Metropolitan areas</span></h4>

<td>2.2 million</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><a name="Migration_and_ethnicity" id="Migration_and_ethnicity"></a></p>
<h3><span class="editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Migration and ethnicity">edit</a>]</span> <span class="mw-headline">Migration and ethnicity</span></h3>
<p>Italy's position in Europe and the northern Mediterranean basin meant many influences, invasions and migrations over thousands of years. As a result, besides the ancient <a href="/wiki/Italic_peoples" title="Italic peoples">Italic peoples</a>, the Italian peninsula has been influenced by <a href="/wiki/Etruscan_civilization" title="Etruscan civilization">Etruscan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a>, ancient <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gallic" title="Gallic">Gallic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celt" title="Celt">Celtic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Normans" title="Normans">Norman</a> <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catalan_people" title="Catalan people">Catalan</a> peoples who either colonised, invaded or plundered Italy over the past 3,000 years.</p>
<p>During the nineteenth and twentieth centuries, Italy was a major source of immigrants to the Americas, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and other countries in <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>. However, Italy is now a destination for immigrants from all over the world with <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>, and Asia being the chief areas. At the beginning of 2006, foreigners comprised 4.56% of the population or 2,670,514<a href="http://demo.istat.it/str2005/index.html" class="external autonumber" title="http://demo.istat.it/str2005/index.html" rel="nofollow">[14]</a> people, an increase of 268,357 or 10 percent from the previous year. In many northern Italian cities, like <a href="/wiki/Padua" title="Padua">Padua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Brescia" title="Brescia">Brescia</a>, migrants make up a significant portion of the population.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/Image:Torino-panoramadaicappuccini.jpg" class="internal" title="Turin"><img alt="Turin" longdesc="/wiki/Image:Torino-panoramadaicappuccini.jpg" class="thumbimage" src="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Torino-panoramadaicappuccini.jpg/250px-Torino-panoramadaicappuccini.jpg" width="250" height="178" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify" style="float:right"><a href="/wiki/Image:Torino-panoramadaicappuccini.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="/skins-1.5/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Turin" title="Turin">Turin</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:502px;"><a href="/wiki/Image:Napoli.jpg" class="internal" title="Naples"><img alt="Naples" longdesc="/wiki/Image:Napoli.jpg" class="thumbimage" src="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Napoli.jpg/500px-Napoli.jpg" width="500" height="140" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify" style="float:right"><a href="/wiki/Image:Napoli.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="/skins-1.5/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The most recent wave of migration has been from Eastern Europe, replacing North Africans as a major source of migrants. As of 2006, some 1,025,874 Eastern Europeans live in Italy, 40% of the total population of migrants in Italy. The five largest foreign nationalities in Italy are: <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albanian</a> (348,813), <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Moroccan</a> (319,537), <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romanian</a> (297,570), <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Chinese</a> (127,822), and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukrainian</a> (107,188).<sup id="_ref-demographics_0" class="reference"><a href="#_note-demographics" title="">[10]</a></sup></p>

<p><sup id="_ref-demographics_1" class="reference"><a href="#_note-demographics" title="">[10]</a></sup> <a name="Religion" id="Religion"></a></p>
<h3><span class="editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a>]</span> <span class="mw-headline">Religion</span></h3>
<dl>
<dd>
<div class="noprint"><i>Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Italy" title="Religion in Italy">Religion in Italy</a></i></div>
</dd>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/Image:StPetersDomePD.jpg" class="internal" title="Saint Peter's Basilica in Rome, the largest church in Christianity"><img alt="Saint Peter's Basilica in Rome, the largest church in Christianity" longdesc="/wiki/Image:StPetersDomePD.jpg" class="thumbimage" src="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/StPetersDomePD.jpg/150px-StPetersDomePD.jpg" width="150" height="218" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify" style="float:right"><a href="/wiki/Image:StPetersDomePD.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="/skins-1.5/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter%27s_Basilica" title="Saint Peter's Basilica">Saint Peter's Basilica</a> in Rome, the largest church in Christianity</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a> is by far the largest religion in the country. Although the Catholic Church is no longer officially the <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a>, it still plays a role in the nation's political affairs, partly due to the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>'s location in Rome. 87.8% of Italians identified as <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> <a href="http://www.corriere.it/Primo_Piano/Cronache/2006/01_Gennaio/17/cattolici.shtml" class="external autonumber" title="http://www.corriere.it/Primo_Piano/Cronache/2006/01_Gennaio/17/cattolici.shtml" rel="nofollow">[15]</a>, although only about one-third of these described themselves as active members (36.8%).</p>
<p>Other <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> groups in Italy include more than 700,000 <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Christians</a> <a href="http://www.ortodossia.it/it.html" class="external autonumber" title="http://www.ortodossia.it/it.html" rel="nofollow">[16]</a>, including 470,000 newcomers <span class="PDFlink"><a href="http://www.db.caritas.glauco.it/caritas/dati/news/2004-05/25/Scheda.pdf" class="external autonumber" title="http://www.db.caritas.glauco.it/caritas/dati/news/2004-05/25/Scheda.pdf" rel="nofollow">[17]</a></span><span style="font-size:smaller;"><a href="/wiki/Portable_Document_Format" title="Portable Document Format">PDF</a>&#160;(65.4&#160;<a href="/wiki/Kibibyte" title="Kibibyte">KiB</a>)</span> and some 180,000 <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Church" title="Greek Orthodox Church">Greek Orthodox</a>, 550,000 <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelicals</a> (0.8%), of whom 400,000 are members of the <a href="/wiki/Assemblies_of_God" title="Assemblies of God">Assemblies of God</a>, 235,685 <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> (0.04%) <a href="http://www.cesnur.org/religioni_italia/t/testimoni_geova_02.htm" class="external autonumber" title="http://www.cesnur.org/religioni_italia/t/testimoni_geova_02.htm" rel="nofollow">[18]</a>, 30,000 <a href="/wiki/Waldensians" title="Waldensians">Waldensians</a> <a href="http://www.chiesavaldese.org/pages/storia/dove_viviamo.php" class="external autonumber" title="http://www.chiesavaldese.org/pages/storia/dove_viviamo.php" rel="nofollow">[19]</a>, 25,000 <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventists" title="Seventh-day Adventists">Seventh-day Adventists</a>, 22,000 <a href="/wiki/Mormons" title="Mormons">Mormons</a>, 15,000 <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a> (plus some 5,000 Free Baptists), 7,000 <a href="/wiki/Lutherans" title="Lutherans">Lutherans</a>, 5,000 <a href="/wiki/Methodists" title="Methodists">Methodists</a> (affiliated to the Waldensian Church) <a href="http://www.fedevangelica.it/fcei/fcei041.asp#celi" class="external autonumber" title="http://www.fedevangelica.it/fcei/fcei041.asp#celi" rel="nofollow">[20]</a>. The country's oldest religious minority is the <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Jewish</a> community, comprising roughly 45,000 people. It is no longer the largest non-Christian group.</p>
<p>As a result of significant immigration from other parts of the world, some 825,000 <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> <a href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/europe/4385768.stm" class="external autonumber" title="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/europe/4385768.stm" rel="nofollow">[21]</a> (1.4%) live in Italy, though only 50,000 are <a href="/wiki/Italian_Citizenship" title="Italian Citizenship">Italian citizens</a>. In addition, there are 110,000 <a href="/wiki/Buddhists" title="Buddhists">Buddhists</a> (0.2%) <a href="http://www.buddhismo.it/ente.htm" class="external autonumber" title="http://www.buddhismo.it/ente.htm" rel="nofollow">[22]</a> <a href="http://www.sgi-italia.org/chi/ibisg.html" class="external autonumber" title="http://www.sgi-italia.org/chi/ibisg.html" rel="nofollow">[23]</a> <span class="PDFlink"><a href="http://www.db.caritas.glauco.it/caritas/dati/news/2004-05/25/Scheda.pdf" class="external autonumber" title="http://www.db.caritas.glauco.it/caritas/dati/news/2004-05/25/Scheda.pdf" rel="nofollow">[24]</a></span><span style="font-size:smaller;"><a href="/wiki/Portable_Document_Format" title="Portable Document Format">PDF</a>&#160;(65.4&#160;<a href="/wiki/Kibibyte" title="Kibibyte">KiB</a>)</span>, 70,000 <a href="/wiki/Sikh" title="Sikh">Sikhs</a> <a href="http://www.etnomedia.org/14.htm" class="external autonumber" title="http://www.etnomedia.org/14.htm" rel="nofollow">[25]</a>, and 70,000 <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindus</a> (0.1%) in Italy.</p>
<dl>
<dd><span class="boilerplate seealso"><i>See also: <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Italy" title="Christianity in Italy">Christianity in Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Italy" title="Islam in Italy">Islam in Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jews_in_Italy" title="Jews in Italy">Jews in Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Italy" title="Buddhism in Italy">Buddhism in Italy</a>,&#160;and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Italian_politicians_belonging_to_a_religious_minority" title="List of Italian politicians belonging to a religious minority">List of Italian politicians belonging to a religious minority</a></i></span></dd>
</dl>
<p><a name="Economy" id="Economy"></a></p>
<h2><span class="editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a>]</span> <span class="mw-headline">Economy</span></h2>
<dl>
<dd>
<div class="noprint"><i>Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Italy" title="Economy of Italy">Economy of Italy</a></i></div>
</dd>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/Image:IMG_4458_-_Milano_-_La_Borsa_-_Foto_di_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_-_20_jan_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="The Borsa Italiana, based in Milan, is Italy's main stock exchange with a capitalisation of $ 890 billion."><img alt="The Borsa Italiana, based in Milan, is Italy's main stock exchange with a capitalisation of $ 890 billion." longdesc="/wiki/Image:IMG_4458_-_Milano_-_La_Borsa_-_Foto_di_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_-_20_jan_2007.jpg" class="thumbimage" src="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/IMG_4458_-_Milano_-_La_Borsa_-_Foto_di_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_-_20_jan_2007.jpg/250px-IMG_4458_-_Milano_-_La_Borsa_-_Foto_di_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_-_20_jan_2007.jpg" width="250" height="166" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify" style="float:right"><a href="/wiki/Image:IMG_4458_-_Milano_-_La_Borsa_-_Foto_di_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_-_20_jan_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="/skins-1.5/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Borsa_Italiana" title="Borsa Italiana">Borsa Italiana</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>, is Italy's main <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a> with a capitalisation of $ 890 billion.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the nominal GDP calculations, Italy was ranked as the seventh largest economy in the world in 2006, behind the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peoples_Republic_of_China" title="Peoples Republic of China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">UK</a>, and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, and the fourth largest in Europe. According to the OECD, in 2004 Italy was the world's sixth-largest exporter of manufactured goods. This <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalistic</a> economy remains divided into a developed industrial north, dominated by private companies, and a less developed <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agricultural</a> south. Italy's economy has an "underground" sector that is not included in the official data, which has recently been calculated by the Ministry of Finance to account for something close to 1/6 of the official GDP.</p>
<p>Most raw materials needed by industry and more than 75% of energy requirements are imported. Over the past decade, Italy has pursued a tight fiscal policy in order to meet the requirements of the <a href="/wiki/Economic_and_Monetary_Union_of_the_European_Union" title="Economic and Monetary Union of the European Union">Economic and Monetary Union</a> and has benefited from lower interest and inflation rates. Italy joined the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">Euro</a> from its introduction in 1999.</p>
<p>Italy's economic performance has at times lagged behind that of its <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a> partners, and the current government has enacted numerous short-term reforms aimed at improving competitiveness and long-term growth. It has moved slowly, however, on implementing certain structural reforms favoured by economists, such as lightening the high tax burden and overhauling Italy's rigid labour market and expensive <a href="/wiki/Pension" title="Pension">pension</a> system, because of the current economic slowdown and opposition from <a href="/wiki/Labor_union" title="Labor union">labour unions</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/Image:Ferrari_599.JPG" class="internal" title="The new Ferrari 599 GTB Fiorano"><img alt="The new Ferrari 599 GTB Fiorano" longdesc="/wiki/Image:Ferrari_599.JPG" class="thumbimage" src="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Ferrari_599.JPG/200px-Ferrari_599.JPG" width="200" height="157" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify" style="float:right"><a href="/wiki/Image:Ferrari_599.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="/skins-1.5/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
The new <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_599_GTB_Fiorano" title="Ferrari 599 GTB Fiorano">Ferrari 599 GTB Fiorano</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Italy has a smaller number of world class multinational corporations than other economies of comparable size. Instead, the country's main economic strength has been its large base of small and medium size companies. Some of these companies manufacture products that are technologically moderately advanced and therefore face increasing competition from China and other emerging Asian economies which are able to undercut them on labour costs. These Italian companies are responding to the Asian competition by concentrating on products with a higher technological content, taking advantage of the technological potential of the country and the cultural tradition of high-quality products, while moving lower-tech manufacturing to plants in countries where labour is less expensive. The small average size of Italian companies remains a limiting factor, and the government has been working to encourage integration and mergers and to reform the rigid regulations that have traditionally been an obstacle to the development of larger corporations in the country.</p>
<p>Italy's major exports are motor vehicles (<a href="/wiki/Fiat_Group" title="Fiat Group">Fiat Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aprilia" title="Aprilia">Aprilia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ducati" title="Ducati">Ducati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piaggio" title="Piaggio">Piaggio</a>) chemicals, petrochemicals and electric goods (<a href="/wiki/Eni_S.p.A." title="Eni S.p.A.">Eni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enel_%28energy%29" title="Enel (energy)">Enel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edison" title="Edison">Edison</a>), aerospace and defence tech (<a href="/wiki/Alenia" title="Alenia">Alenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agusta" title="Agusta">Agusta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finmeccanica" title="Finmeccanica">Finmeccanica</a>), firearms (<a href="/wiki/Beretta" title="Beretta">Beretta</a>)&#160;; but the country's more famous exports are in the fields of food industry (<a href="/wiki/Parmalat" title="Parmalat">Parmalat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barilla_Group" title="Barilla Group">Barilla Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martini_%26_Rossi" title="Martini &amp; Rossi">Martini &amp; Rossi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Campari" title="Campari">Campari</a>), fashion (<a href="/wiki/Armani" title="Armani">Armani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valentino" title="Valentino">Valentino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benetton" title="Benetton">Benetton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prada" title="Prada">Prada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luxottica" title="Luxottica">Luxottica</a>), luxury vehicles (<a href="/wiki/Ferrari" title="Ferrari">Ferrari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maserati" title="Maserati">Maserati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lamborghini" title="Lamborghini">Lamborghini</a>) and motoryachts (<a href="/wiki/Ferretti_Group" title="Ferretti Group">Ferretti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azimut" title="Azimut">Azimut</a>).</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Italy" title="Tourism in Italy">Tourism</a> is very important to the Italian economy. With over 37 million tourists a year, Italy is <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_Rankings" title="World Tourism Rankings">ranked</a> as the fifth major tourist destination in the world.<sup id="_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#_note-6" title="">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p><a name="Transport" id="Transport"></a></p>
<h2><span class="editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a>]</span> <span class="mw-headline">Transport</span></h2>
<dl>
<dd>
<div class="noprint"><i>Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Italy" title="Transport in Italy">Transport in Italy</a></i></div>
</dd>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/Image:DSC02042_Uscita_Stazione_centrale_di_Milano_-_Foto_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_1-1-2007.jpg" class="internal" title="ETR 500 at Milan Central Station"><img alt="ETR 500 at Milan Central Station" longdesc="/wiki/Image:DSC02042_Uscita_Stazione_centrale_di_Milano_-_Foto_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_1-1-2007.jpg" class="thumbimage" src="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/DSC02042_Uscita_Stazione_centrale_di_Milano_-_Foto_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_1-1-2007.jpg/250px-DSC02042_Uscita_Stazione_centrale_di_Milano_-_Foto_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_1-1-2007.jpg" width="250" height="188" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify" style="float:right"><a href="/wiki/Image:DSC02042_Uscita_Stazione_centrale_di_Milano_-_Foto_Giovanni_Dall%27Orto_1-1-2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="/skins-1.5/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/ETR_500" title="ETR 500">ETR 500</a> at <a href="/wiki/Milan_Central_Station" title="Milan Central Station">Milan Central Station</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Railway" title="Railway">railway</a> network in Italy totals 19,394 kilometres (12,051 <a href="/wiki/Mi" title="Mi">mi</a>), ranking the country 16th in the world,<sup id="_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#_note-7" title="">[12]</a></sup> and is operated by <a href="/wiki/Ferrovie_dello_Stato" title="Ferrovie dello Stato">Ferrovie dello Stato</a>. High speed trains include <a href="/wiki/ETR" title="ETR">ETR</a>-class trains, of which the <a href="/wiki/ETR_500" title="ETR 500">ETR 500</a> travels at 300 km/h (186 mph).</p>
<p>In 1991 <a href="/wiki/Treno_Alta_Velocit%C3%A0" title="Treno Alta Velocità">Treno Alta Velocità SpA</a> was created, a <a href="/wiki/Special_purpose_entity" title="Special purpose entity">special purpose entity</a> owned by <a href="/wiki/Rete_Ferroviaria_Italiana" title="Rete Ferroviaria Italiana">RFI</a> (itself owned by <a href="/wiki/Ferrovie_dello_Stato" title="Ferrovie dello Stato">Ferrovie dello Stato</a>)for the planning and construction of <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail" title="High-speed rail">high-speed rail</a> lines along Italy's most important and saturated transport routes. These lines are often referred as "TAV" lines. The purpose of TAV construction is to aid travel along Italy's most saturated and used rail lines and to add tracks to these lines, namely the Milan-Naples and Turin-Milan-Venice corridors. One of the focuses of the project is to turn the rail network of Italy into a modern and high-tech passenger rail system in accordance with updated <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> rail standards. A secondary purpose is to introduce <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail" title="High-speed rail">high-speed rail</a> to the country and its high-priority corridors. An important consideration of the lines is to improve travel times, train frequency, and safety. When demand on regular lines is lessened with the opening of dedicated high-speed lines, those regular lines will be used primarily for low-speed regional rail service and freight trains. With these ideas realised, the Italian train network can be integrated with other European rail networks, particularly the French <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGV</a>, German <a href="/wiki/InterCityExpress" title="InterCityExpress">ICE</a>, and Spanish <a href="/wiki/AVE" title="AVE">AVE</a> systems.</p>
<p>There are approximately 654,676 kilometres (406,000 mi) of serviceable roadway in Italy, including 6,957 km (4,300 mi) of expressways.</p>
<p>There are approximately 133 airports in Italy, including the two <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">hubs</a> of <a href="/wiki/Malpensa_International_Airport" title="Malpensa International Airport">Malpensa International</a> (near Milan) and <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_Da_Vinci_International_Airport" title="Leonardo Da Vinci International Airport">Leonardo Da Vinci International</a> (near Rome).</p>
<p>There are 27 major ports in Italy, the largest is in <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a>, which is also the second largest in the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>, after <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a>. 2,400 kilometres (1,500 mi) of waterways traverse Italy.</p>
<p><a name="Culture" id="Culture"></a></p>
<h2><span class="editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a>]</span> <span class="mw-headline">Culture</span></h2>
<dl>
<dd>
<div class="noprint"><i>Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Italy" title="Culture of Italy">Culture of Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_literature" title="Italian literature">Italian literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Italy" title="Music of Italy">Music of Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Italy" title="Sport in Italy">Sport in Italy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Italy" title="Cinema of Italy">Cinema of Italy</a></i></div>
</dd>
<dd><i>Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Italian_painters" title="List of Italian painters">List of Italian painters</a></i></dd>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/Image:Sanzio_00.jpg" class="internal" title="Raffaello"><img alt="Raffaello" longdesc="/wiki/Image:Sanzio_00.jpg" class="thumbimage" src="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Sanzio_00.jpg/150px-Sanzio_00.jpg" width="150" height="203" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify" style="float:right"><a href="/wiki/Image:Sanzio_00.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="/skins-1.5/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Raffaello" title="Raffaello">Raffaello</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Italy, as a state, did not exist until the unification of the country came to a conclusion in the year 1861. Due to this comparatively late unification, and the historical autonomy of the many regions that comprise the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Peninsula" title="Italian Peninsula">Italian Peninsula</a>, many traditions and customs that we now recognise as distinctly Italian can be identified by their regions of origin, which further reflects the influence of the many different peoples that occupied those areas, and of the importance of religion, especially <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a>. Despite the pronounced political and social isolation of these regions that prevailed throughout Italy's history, Italy's contributions to the cultural and historical heritage of <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> remain immense. In fact, Italy is home to the greatest number of <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Europe#Italy" title="List of World Heritage Sites in Europe">World Heritage Sites</a> (41) to date.</p>
<p><a name="Visual_Art" id="Visual_Art"></a></p>
<h3><span class="editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Visual Art">edit</a>]</span> <span class="mw-headline">Visual Art</span></h3>
<p>Italy has been a seminal place for many important artistic and intellectual movements that spread throughout Europe and beyond, including the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a>. Perhaps Italy's greatest cultural achievements lie in its long artistic heritage, which is often validated through the names of <a href="/wiki/Michelangelo" title="Michelangelo">Michelangelo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a>, <a href="/wiki/Donatello" title="Donatello">Donatello</a>, <a href="/wiki/Botticelli" title="Botticelli">Botticelli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fra_Angelico" title="Fra Angelico">Fra Angelico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tintoretto" title="Tintoretto">Tintoretto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caravaggio" title="Caravaggio">Caravaggio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bernini" title="Bernini">Bernini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Titian" title="Titian">Titian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Raphael" title="Raphael">Raphael</a>, among many others. Beyond art, Italy's contributions to the realms of literature, science, and music cannot be overlooked.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/Image:DanteDetail.jpg" class="internal" title="Dante, author of the Divine Comedy"><img alt="Dante, author of the Divine Comedy" longdesc="/wiki/Image:DanteDetail.jpg" class="thumbimage" src="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f7/DanteDetail.jpg/200px-DanteDetail.jpg" width="200" height="130" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify" style="float:right"><a href="/wiki/Image:DanteDetail.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="/skins-1.5/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Dante" title="Dante">Dante</a>, author of the <a href="/wiki/Divine_Comedy" title="Divine Comedy">Divine Comedy</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a name="Literature" id="Literature"></a></p>
<h3><span class="editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a>]</span> <span class="mw-headline">Literature</span></h3>
<p>With the basis of the modern <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian language</a> established through the eminent <a href="/wiki/Florentine" title="Florentine">Florentine</a> poet, <a href="/wiki/Dante_Alighieri" title="Dante Alighieri">Dante Alighieri</a>, whose greatest work, the <a href="/wiki/Divina_Commedia" title="Divina Commedia">Divina Commedia</a>, is often considered the foremost literary statement produced in Europe during the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> and one of the greatest works of world literature ever, there is no shortage of celebrated literary figures; the writers and poets <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Boccaccio" title="Giovanni Boccaccio">Boccaccio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giacomo_Leopardi" title="Giacomo Leopardi">Giacomo Leopardi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alessandro_Manzoni" title="Alessandro Manzoni">Alessandro Manzoni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tasso" title="Tasso">Tasso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludovico_Ariosto" title="Ludovico Ariosto">Ludovico Ariosto</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Petrarca" title="Francesco Petrarca">Petrarch</a>, whose best known vehicle of expression, the <a href="/wiki/Sonnet" title="Sonnet">sonnet</a>, was invented in Italy. Prominent philosophers include <a href="/wiki/Giordano_Bruno" title="Giordano Bruno">Bruno</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ficino" title="Ficino">Ficino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machiavelli" title="Machiavelli">Machiavelli</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Giambattista_Vico" title="Giambattista Vico">Vico</a>. Modern literary figures and Nobel laureates are nationalist poet <a href="/wiki/Giosu%C3%A8_Carducci" title="Giosuè Carducci">Giosuè Carducci</a> in 1906, realist writer <a href="/wiki/Grazia_Deledda" title="Grazia Deledda">Grazia Deledda</a> in 1926, modern theatre author <a href="/wiki/Luigi_Pirandello" title="Luigi Pirandello">Luigi Pirandello</a> in 1936, poets <a href="/wiki/Salvatore_Quasimodo" title="Salvatore Quasimodo">Salvatore Quasimodo</a> in 1959 and <a href="/wiki/Eugenio_Montale" title="Eugenio Montale">Eugenio Montale</a> in 1975, satiryst and theatre author <a href="/wiki/Dario_Fo" title="Dario Fo">Dario Fo</a> in 1997.</p>
<p><a name="Science" id="Science"></a></p>
<h3><span class="editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Science">edit</a>]</span> <span class="mw-headline">Science</span></h3>
<p>In science, <a href="/wiki/Galileo_Galilei" title="Galileo Galilei">Galileo Galilei</a> made considerable advancements toward the <a href="/wiki/Scientific_revolution" title="Scientific revolution">scientific revolution</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a> was the quintessential <a href="/wiki/Polymath" title="Polymath">Renaissance Man</a>. Italy has been the home of many great scientists and inventors: the physicist <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Fermi" title="Enrico Fermi">Fermi</a>, one of the fathers of <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">quantum theory</a> and head of the <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Project" title="Manhattan Project">Manhattan Project</a>; the astronomer <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Domenico_Cassini" title="Giovanni Domenico Cassini">Cassini</a>; the physicist <a href="/wiki/Alessandro_Volta" title="Alessandro Volta">Volta</a>, inventor of the <a href="/wiki/Electric_battery" title="Electric battery">electric battery</a>; the mathematicians <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Louis_Lagrange" title="Joseph Louis Lagrange">Lagrange</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fibonacci" title="Fibonacci">Fibonacci</a>; Nobel Prize in Physics laureate <a href="/wiki/Guglielmo_Marconi" title="Guglielmo Marconi">Marconi</a>, inventor of the <a href="/wiki/Radio" title="Radio">radio</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Meucci" title="Antonio Meucci">Antonio Meucci</a>, disputable inventor of the <a href="/wiki/Telephone" title="Telephone">telephone</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/Image:Verdi.jpg" class="internal" title="Giuseppe Verdi"><img alt="Giuseppe Verdi" longdesc="/wiki/Image:Verdi.jpg" class="thumbimage" src="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Verdi.jpg/150px-Verdi.jpg" width="150" height="194" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify" style="float:right"><a href="/wiki/Image:Verdi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="/skins-1.5/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Verdi" title="Giuseppe Verdi">Giuseppe Verdi</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a name="Music" id="Music"></a></p>
<h3><span class="editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a>]</span> <span class="mw-headline">Music</span></h3>
<p>From <a href="/wiki/Italian_folk_music" title="Italian folk music">folk music</a> to <a href="/wiki/European_classical_music" title="European classical music">classical</a>, music has always played an important role in Italian culture. Having given birth to <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">opera</a>, for example, Italy provides many of the very foundations of the classical music tradition. Some of the instruments that are often associated with classical music, including the <a href="/wiki/Piano" title="Piano">piano</a> and <a href="/wiki/Violin" title="Violin">violin</a>, were invented in Italy, and many of the existing classical music forms can trace their roots back to innovations of sixteenth and seventeenth century Italian music (such as the <a href="/wiki/Symphony" title="Symphony">symphony</a>, <a href="/wiki/Concerto" title="Concerto">concerto</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sonata" title="Sonata">sonata</a>). Some of Italy's most famous composers include the Renaissance composers <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Pierluigi_da_Palestrina" title="Giovanni Pierluigi da Palestrina">Palestrina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Claudio_Monteverdi" title="Claudio Monteverdi">Monteverdi</a>, the Baroque composers <a href="/wiki/Arcangelo_Corelli" title="Arcangelo Corelli">Corelli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Vivaldi" title="Antonio Vivaldi">Vivaldi</a>, the Classical composers <a href="/wiki/Niccol%C3%B2_Paganini" title="Niccolò Paganini">Paganini</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gioacchino_Rossini" title="Gioacchino Rossini">Rossini</a>, and the Romantic composers <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Verdi" title="Giuseppe Verdi">Verdi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Giacomo_Puccini" title="Giacomo Puccini">Puccini</a>. Modern Italian composers such as <a href="/wiki/Luciano_Berio" title="Luciano Berio">Berio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luigi_Nono" title="Luigi Nono">Nono</a> proved significant in the development of experimental and electronic music.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/Image:Italy_FIFA2006_winner.jpg" class="internal" title="The Azzurri exulting after they won FIFA 2006 Germany World Cup"><img alt="The Azzurri exulting after they won FIFA 2006 Germany World Cup" longdesc="/wiki/Image:Italy_FIFA2006_winner.jpg" class="thumbimage" src="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/59/Italy_FIFA2006_winner.jpg/200px-Italy_FIFA2006_winner.jpg" width="200" height="158" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify" style="float:right"><a href="/wiki/Image:Italy_FIFA2006_winner.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="/skins-1.5/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Azzurri" title="Azzurri">Azzurri</a> exulting after they won <a href="/wiki/FIFA_2006" title="FIFA 2006">FIFA 2006</a> Germany World Cup</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a name="Sport" id="Sport"></a></p>
<h3><span class="editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a>]</span> <span class="mw-headline">Sport</span></h3>
<p>Italians are renowned for their love of <a href="/wiki/Sports" title="Sports">sports</a>. Their zeal for sports events is, indeed, no less than legendary; from the <a href="/wiki/Gladiator" title="Gladiator">Gladiatorial games</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Ancient Rome</a>, to the <a href="/wiki/Stadio_Olimpico" title="Stadio Olimpico">Stadio Olimpico</a> of contemporary Rome, where prestigious football clubs compete regularly, the impact that sports has had on Italian culture is enduring and undeniable. Towards the alps, the popularity of <a href="/wiki/Winter_sports" title="Winter sports">winter sports</a> grows, with many Italians from that region competing in international games and Olympic venues. Moving downwards the peninsula, the disparity between participation in sports becomes less regional. The incorporation of sports in many Italian festivities like <a href="/wiki/Palio" title="Palio">Palio</a> (see also <a href="/wiki/Palio_di_Siena" title="Palio di Siena">Palio di Siena</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Gondola" title="Gondola">Gondola</a> race (<a href="/wiki/Regatta" title="Regatta">regatta</a>) that takes place in Venice on the first Sunday of September, affirms the role sports play in everyday Italian life. Popular sports include <a href="/wiki/Football_%28soccer%29" title="Football (soccer)">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> (2nd national team sport since the '50s), <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Union" title="Rugby Union">rugby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">cycling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hockey" title="Hockey">hockey</a> (mainly in Milan, Trentino-Alto Adige and Veneto) and <a href="/wiki/F1" title="F1">F1</a> (second most popular sport, a sport which shares its renown with a staple of Italian design, <a href="/wiki/Ferrari" title="Ferrari">Ferrari</a>), among others.</p>
<p><a name="Languages" id="Languages"></a></p>
<h2><span class="editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a>]</span> <span class="mw-headline">Languages</span></h2>
<dl>
<dd>
<div class="noprint"><i>Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Italy" title="Languages of Italy">Languages of Italy</a></i></div>
</dd>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/Image:Gondola.arp.750pix.jpg" class="internal" title="Gondolas in Venice; Rialto Bridge in background"><img alt="Gondolas in Venice; Rialto Bridge in background" longdesc="/wiki/Image:Gondola.arp.750pix.jpg" class="thumbimage" src="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Gondola.arp.750pix.jpg/300px-Gondola.arp.750pix.jpg" width="300" height="225" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify" style="float:right"><a href="/wiki/Image:Gondola.arp.750pix.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="/skins-1.5/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Gondola" title="Gondola">Gondolas</a> in <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>; <a href="/wiki/Rialto_Bridge" title="Rialto Bridge">Rialto Bridge</a> in background</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/Image:Italy_-_Forms_of_Dialect.jpg" class="internal" title="Dialects and languages of Italy"><img alt="Dialects and languages of Italy" longdesc="/wiki/Image:Italy_-_Forms_of_Dialect.jpg" class="thumbimage" src="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Italy_-_Forms_of_Dialect.jpg/300px-Italy_-_Forms_of_Dialect.jpg" width="300" height="350" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify" style="float:right"><a href="/wiki/Image:Italy_-_Forms_of_Dialect.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="/skins-1.5/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
Dialects and languages of Italy</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The official language of Italy is <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Standard Italian</a>, a descendant of <a href="/wiki/Tuscan_dialect" title="Tuscan dialect">Tuscan dialect</a> and a direct descendant of <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>. Some 75 percent of Italian words are of Latin origin.</p>
<p>When Italy was unified in 1861 Italian existed mainly as a <a href="/wiki/Literary_language" title="Literary language">literary language</a>. Many <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance</a> <a href="/wiki/Regional_language" title="Regional language">regional languages</a> were spoken throughout the Italian peninsula (<a href="/wiki/Italian_dialects" title="Italian dialects">Italian dialects</a>), with many local variants.</p>
<p>Following Italian unification <a href="/wiki/Massimo_Taparelli%2C_marquis_d%27Azeglio" title="Massimo Taparelli, marquis d'Azeglio">Massimo Taparelli, marquis d'Azeglio</a>, one of <a href="/wiki/Camillo_Benso%2C_conte_di_Cavour" title="Camillo Benso, conte di Cavour">Cavour's</a> ministers, is said to have stated that having created Italy, all that remained was to create Italians (a <a href="/wiki/National_identity" title="National identity">national identity</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Tuscan_dialect" title="Tuscan dialect">Tuscan dialect</a> (or <i>Florentine dialect</i>) spoken in <a href="/wiki/Tuscany" title="Tuscany">Tuscany</a> was promoted as the standard dialect in large part due to its literary heritage (<a href="/wiki/Dante_Alighieri" title="Dante Alighieri">Dante's</a> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Divine_Comedy" title="The Divine Comedy">Divine Comedy</a></i> is often credited with the emergence of the Tuscan dialect as standard). <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Bembo" title="Pietro Bembo">Pietro Bembo</a>, influenced by <a href="/wiki/Petrarch" title="Petrarch">Petrarch</a>, also promoted Tuscan as the standard literary language (<i>volgare illustre</i>). The spread of the <a href="/wiki/Printing_press" title="Printing press">printing press</a> and <a href="/wiki/Literary_movement" title="Literary movement">literary movements</a> (such as petrarchism and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bembismo&amp;action=edit" class="new" title="Bembismo">bembismo</a>) also furthern Italian standardization.asp</p>
<p>The estbalishment of a national education system led to a decrease in variation in the languages spoken across the country. Standardization was also hastened in the 1960s because of economic growth leading to the popularization of <a href="/wiki/Television" title="Television">television</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Public_broadcasting" title="Public broadcasting">state broadcaster</a> <a href="/wiki/RAI" title="RAI">RAI</a> set an Italian standard).</p>
<p>Today, despite regional variations in the form of <a href="/wiki/Accent_%28linguistics%29" title="Accent (linguistics)">accents</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vowel" title="Vowel">vowel</a> emphasis, Italian dialects are almost always <a href="/wiki/Mutual_intelligibility" title="Mutual intelligibility">mutual intelligible</a>. Nevertheless <a href="/wiki/Variety_%28linguistics%29" title="Variety (linguistics)">variety</a> remains, and is often used in <a href="/wiki/Idiom" title="Idiom">idioms</a> and <a href="/wiki/Traditional_music" title="Traditional music">folk songs</a>.</p>
<p>Some languages spoken in Italy are not considered Italian dialects but are different languages entirely, such as <a href="/wiki/Venetian_language" title="Venetian language">Venetian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neapolitan_language" title="Neapolitan language">Neapolitan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sicilian_language" title="Sicilian language">Sicilian</a> and other Gallo-Italian languages of the north.</p>
<p>In addition to the various regional linguistic varieties and dialects of standard Italian, a number of languages enjoying some form of official recognition are spoken:</p>
<ul>
<li>In the north, the province of <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Bolzano-Bozen" title="Autonomous Province of Bolzano-Bozen">Bolzano-Bozen</a> has a majority <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>-speaking population (<a href="/wiki/Upper_German" title="Upper German">Upper German</a>). This area was taken from <a href="/wiki/Austro-Hungary" title="Austro-Hungary">Austro-Hungary</a> and given to Italy under the terms of the 1919 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Saint-Germain-en-Laye_%281919%29" title="Treaty of Saint-Germain-en-Laye (1919)">Treaty of Saint-Germain-en-Laye</a> after the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. Some German-speaking communities also exist in other parts of <a href="/wiki/North_Italy" title="North Italy">north Italy</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cimbrian_language" title="Cimbrian language">Cimbrian</a> is a German language related to <a href="/wiki/Austro-Bavarian" title="Austro-Bavarian">Austro-Bavarian</a> spoken in some parts of <a href="/wiki/Veneto" title="Veneto">Veneto</a> (<a href="/wiki/Asiago" title="Asiago">Asiago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luserna" title="Luserna">Luserna</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Walser" title="Walser">Walsers</a> in Val'Aosta (<a href="/wiki/Gressoney-La-Trinit%C3%A9" title="Gressoney-La-Trinité">Gressoney</a>). In total some 300,000 or so Italians speak German as their first language. Some identify themselves as <a href="/wiki/Austrian_people" title="Austrian people">ethnic Austrians</a>.</li>
<li>Some 120,000 people live in the <a href="/wiki/Aosta_Valley" title="Aosta Valley">Aosta Valley</a> region, where a dialect of <a href="/wiki/Franco-Proven%C3%A7al_language" title="Franco-Provençal language">Franco-Provençal</a> is spoken that is similar to dialects spoken in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>. About 1,400 people living in two isolated towns in <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Foggia" title="Province of Foggia">Foggia</a> speak another dialect of Franco-Provençal.</li>
<li>About 80,000 <a href="/wiki/Slovenian_language" title="Slovenian language">Slovene</a>-speakers live in the north-eastern region of <a href="/wiki/Friuli-Venezia_Giulia" title="Friuli-Venezia Giulia">Friuli-Venezia Giulia</a> near the border with Slovenia.</li>
<li>In the <a href="/wiki/Dolomites" title="Dolomites">Dolomite</a> mountains of <a href="/wiki/Trentino-Alto_Adige/S%C3%BCdtirol" title="Trentino-Alto Adige/Südtirol">Trentino-Alto Adige/Südtirol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Veneto" title="Veneto">Veneto</a> there are some 40,000 speakers of the <a href="/wiki/Rhaeto-Romance_languages" title="Rhaeto-Romance languages">Rhaeto-Romance</a> language <a href="/wiki/Ladin" title="Ladin">Ladin</a>.</li>
<li>A community of 700,000 in <a href="/wiki/Friuli" title="Friuli">Friuli</a> speak <a href="/wiki/Friulian_language" title="Friulian language">Friulian</a>, also a Rhaeto-Romance language.</li>
<li>In the <a href="/wiki/Molise" title="Molise">Molise</a> region of central-south Italy some 4,000 people speak <a href="/wiki/Molise_Croatian_dialect" title="Molise Croatian dialect">Molise Croatian</a>. These are the <a href="/wiki/Molise_Croats" title="Molise Croats">Molise Croats</a>, descendants of a group of people who migrated from the Balkans in the Middle Ages.</li>
<li>Scattered across <a href="/wiki/Southern_Italy" title="Southern Italy">southern Italy</a> (<a href="/wiki/Salento" title="Salento">Salento</a> and <a href="/wiki/Calabria" title="Calabria">Calabria</a>) are some 30,000 <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>-speakers—considered to be the last surviving traces of the region's <a href="/wiki/Magna_Graecia" title="Magna Graecia">Magna Graecia</a> heritage. They speak a Greek dialect, <a href="/wiki/Griko_language" title="Griko language">Griko</a>.</li>
<li>Some 15,000 <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a> speakers reside around the area of <a href="/wiki/Alghero" title="Alghero">Alghero</a> in the north-west corner of <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a>—believed to be the result of a migration of a large group of Catalans from <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Arb%C3%ABresh%C3%AB" title="Arbëreshë">Arbëreshë</a>, of whom there are around 100,000 in southern Italy and in central <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a>, the result of past migrations, are speakers of the Arbëresh dialect of <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>.</li>
<li>Finally, the largest group of non-Italian speakers, some 1.3 million people, are those who speak <a href="/wiki/Sardinian_language" title="Sardinian language">Sardinian</a>, a Romance language which retains many pre-Latin words.</li>
</ul>
<p><a name="Notes" id="Notes"></a></p>
<h2><span class="editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a>]</span> <span class="mw-headline">Notes</span></h2>
<div class="references-small"></div>
<div id="endnoteQRomanian"><sup><small><a href="#refQRomanian" title="">1</a></small></sup> According to Mitrica, an October 2005 Romanian report estimates that 1,061,400 Romanians are living in Italy, constituting 37.2% of 2.8 million immigrants in that country <a href="http://www.evz.ro/eveniment/?news_id=201813" class="external autonumber" title="http://www.evz.ro/eveniment/?news_id=201813" rel="nofollow">[26]</a> but it is unclear how the estimate was made, and therefore whether it should be taken seriously or not.</div>
<div id="endnoteQdialects"><sup><small><a href="#refQdialects" title="">2</a></small></sup> See also (in Italian): <i>L. Lepschy e G. Lepschy, La lingua italiana: storia, varietà d'uso, grammatica, Milano, Bompiani</i></div>
<div id="endnoteQmontblanc"><sup><small><a href="#refQmontblanc" title="">3</a></small></sup> Official French maps show the border detouring south of the main summit, and claim the highest point in Italy is Mont Blanc de Courmayeur (4,748 m), but these are inconsistent with an 1861 convention and topographic watershed analysis.</div>

font-weight:bold;">&#160;·</span> <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Netherlands</a><sup><small>3</small></sup><span style="white-space:nowrap; font-weight:bold;">&#160;·</span> <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a><sup><small>3</small></sup><span style="white-space:nowrap; font-weight:bold;">&#160;·</span> <span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia (FYROM)</a></span><span style="white-space:nowrap; font-weight:bold;">&#160;·</span> <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a><span style="white-space:nowrap; font-weight:bold;">&#160;·</span> <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a><sup><small>1</small></sup><span style="white-space:nowrap; font-weight:bold;">&#160;·</span> <span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a></span><span style="white-space:nowrap; font-weight:bold;">&#160;·</span> <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a><span style="white-space:nowrap; font-weight:bold;">&#160;·</span> <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a><span style="white-space:nowrap; font-weight:bold;">&#160;·</span> <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a><span style="white-space:nowrap; font-weight:bold;">&#160;·</span> <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a><span style="white-space:nowrap; font-weight:bold;">&#160;·</span> <span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a></span><sup><small>3</small></sup><span style="white-space:nowrap; font-weight:bold;">&#160;·</span> <span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a></span></p>
<p><small><sup>1</sup>&#160;Has <a href="/wiki/Transcontinental_country" title="Transcontinental country">majority of its territory</a> in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>.&#160; <sup>2</sup>&#160;Entirely in Asia but having socio-political connections with Europe.&#160; <sup>3</sup>&#160;Has <a href="/wiki/Dependent_territory" title="Dependent territory">dependencies</a> or similar territories outside Europe.</small></p>

<div style="text-align:left; font-size:80%;">
